								1


                WILLIAM FOX OF BRUNSWICK COUNTY, VIRGINIA


           William Fox of Brunswick County, Virginia, (born ca. 1710;
d. 1764) was one of several sons of Henry Fox (2nd) of Brunswick County,
Virginia, and was a brother of Colonel Henry Fox (3rd), who went to
South Carolina.

           William Fox of Brunswick County, Virginia, is of special
interest to the Mississippi Fox family because of the possible connec-
tion with Sarah Harrell, the wife of Henry Fox (born 1768i died 1852),
who was a son of William Fox of Richland County, South Carolina, and a
grandson of Col. Henry Fox of the same county.

           It is thought that this William Fox moved to Brunswick County
about the same time that his father, Henry Fox (2nd), settled there.
They apparently located near where William's brother, Henry Fox (3rd),
had settled previously.

           Dr. J. Ben Robinson of Baltimore, Maryland, a Fox family
historian descended from John Fox, son of Henry and Anne West Fox, has
called attention to the fact that Brunswick County was constructed in
1720, though the organization of its government was delayed until 1732.
(See also Chapter 3, Section 1, of Mr. Steadman's book.)  A courthouse
was built, and a "Commission of the Peace" was appointed, with Henry
Fox (2nd), formerly justice and sheriff of King William County, acting
as Chief Justice.  Dr. Robinson states that Fort Christiana, which was
built in 1714 as a frontier protection, fell within the county, and
when Henry Fox (2nd) moved to Brunswick county in 1731, he probably
settled somewhere near the courthouse and the Fort, which were about six
miles apart.  Land deeds indicate that Henry (3rd) lived near the Fort;
and his brother, William Fox, lived at first on Fontaine Creek, about 15
miles from Henry (3rd), and later lived across the creek on a large
plantation left his wife, Mary Avent Fox, by her father Capt. Thomas
Avent.  Dr. Robinson considers Richard Fox, who lived on the south side
of the Roanoke River at Smith's Creek, about 15 miles from Henry (3rd),
another brother of Henry (3rd) and William Fox.  Mr. Steadman is of the
opinion, as set forth in his work, that he belonged to a different family.

           About 1734 William Fox married Sarah Avent.  Her father, Capt.
Thomas Avent, died in Surry County, Virginia, in 1756.  The following is
a quotation from the work of Dr. Robinson:

           "Col. Thomas Avent died in Surry County in 1756.  In 1763
     the administrator of his estate sold his Brunswick County (then
     Innenburg County) property to Robert Lark who, in turn sold it to
     Richard Fox's son, Jacob Fox, 'whose land it adjoined.'  In 1743


    William Fox bought and occupied land in eastern Brunswick County.
    He was located south of the Meherrin River and situated on the
    west bank of Fountain Run about 18 miles southeast of Fort Chris-
    tiana.  William and Sarah (Avent) Fox had three sons and eight
    daughters, many of whose descendants now live in Greensville,
    Sussex and Southampton Counties, Virginia, and in Halifax and
    Northampton Counties, North Carolina, from whom the writer has
    obtained much valuable information.  It is of peculiar interest
    that Winifred Fox, a granddaughter of William Fox, married James
    Robinson, a nephew of Mrs. Hannah (Williamson) Fox, wife of
    Richard Fox.  The late Miss Kathleen Alsop, for years registrar
    at the College of William and Mary, was of this line."
    [This information was included in unpublished material given to
    Shirley Faucette by Dr. Robinson.]


           Included as exhibits in this section are excerpts from the will
of William Fox of Brunswick County, Virginia, dated December 22,1763, and
recorded January 23, 1764.

           Also included is a list of the children of William and Sarah
Avent Fox prepared by Dr. Robinson showing the probable dates of birth
as indicated by facts known concerning them.


Noona (Unity?) Fox, Daughter of William and Sarah Avent Fox

           Of special interest to Mississippi Foxes is the daughter
listed as "Noona" in the will of William Fox.  It is considered highly
likely by both Dr. Robinson and Mr. Steadman that "Noona" was the nick-
name for a daughter who was named "Unity" and that she is the same
Unity Fox who is shown as marrying John (or William?) Harrell, in
North Carolina, and who may have been the mother of Sarah Harrell
who married Henry Fox (1768-1852).

           For some time it has been thought that Sarah Harrell who
married Henry Fox was probably a daughter of William Harrell, who was
shown in the 1790 census for Richland County, S.C., as "William Harold".
It was further conjectured that this William Harrell was a son of John
Harrell, and that William married Unity Fox.  This supposition was based
on a record given both to Dr. Robinson and Mr. Steadman, which stated:

           "Wm. Harrell (son of Jno.) m Unity Fox N.C."

           This record was one of some 206 separate items about the Fox
family given to Mr. Joseph E. Steadman, Sr., in 1933 by Eloise Weeks
Colson (Mrs. James H. Colson), then of Gainsville, Florida.  Mrs. Colson
was a dauqhter of Anna Cornelia Fox and James S. Weeks, and was a descen-
dant of David Fox, thought to be a grandson or great-grandson of the
David Fox who married Hannah Ball.  Apparently the same 206 items were
given to Dr. J. Ben Robinson by Mrs. Mary Smith Wichter of Tulsa, Okla.,
whose cousin (likely Mrs. Colson) compiled the data.  It was thought by




Dr. Robinson that the items were part of a collection of genealogies in
the Georgia Historical Library, Savannah, Georgia, and possibly a part
of the Habersham Collection.

          A brief search was made at the Georgia Historical Library in
Savannah by Shirley Faucette in July 1970, but at that time the library
was in the process of being moved, and t-he impression was received that
there were unpublished collections which could be searched at another
time which were not available then.  Volumes I, II, and III of the
Joseph Habersham Collection and several supplemental volumes published
by the Georgia D.A.R.'s are contained in the Mississippi Department of
Archives and History Library, but a search of these volumes has not
revealed the above records.  Therefore, it is assumed that these items
are either in the unpublished collections or from another sources, which
to date has not been identified.

          However, published data has recently been found which states
that John Harrell married Unity Fox, and had a son William.

Burch, Harrell, and Allied Families, by Marilu Burch Smallwood and
North Carolina Historical and Genealogical Register, by J. R. B. Hathaway:

          The following information is quoted from various sources by Mrs.
Marilu Burch Smallwood on Page 132 of "Burch, Harrell, and Allied Families,
Volume 1:

    "In Page 127 of 'Happy Heritage' by Cannon, Lewis Harrell is
    mentioned in the first census of the U S (1790) as being the
    head of a family living in Georgetown District, Prince Fred-
    ricks Parish South Carolina....  Happy Heritage claims Lewis to
    have been son of John, but gives no proof, no will, or anything...."

She refers to a will of a Lewis Harrell, naming a son Jacob, and states:

    "John may have had a son Lewis, but not Lewis of the following will....
    Perhaps John Harrell of the following record is the John Harrell
    mentioned in 'Happy Heritage' as the father of Lewis."

Mrs. Smallwood continues on Page 133, quoting from J. R. B. Hathaway's
"North Carolina Historical and Genealogical Register", Volume 2, Page 157,
published in 1901:

    "William Harrell married Mary Harrell (lst cousins) children
    of William and John Harrell, they had a brother Hardy.  An
    ancestors of theirs was Hardy Harrell called grandsire-Harrell.
    They were from Eastern North Carolina but a branch of the
    family went to South Carolina.  They were connected with Mrs.
    Washington's family, supposed to be through the Foxes.  William
    and Mary had one child Agnes who married Jno. Lackland McIntosh
    of McIntosh County, Georgia.  2nd married George Augustus Smith
    reputed to be the grandson of the Earl of Stanhope, his mother
    was Martha Sweeting (both of London)...."



DAR Records:

          Lineage books published by the National Society of the D.A.R.
 contain records of the following members who joined on the service
 record of JOHN HARRELL, whose wife is given as Unity Fox:

    Miss Annie Hornady, born Americus, Georgia, No. 32401
    Miss Laura Nina Hornady, sister of the above, No. 32402
    Mrs. Flora Smith Chapman, born Macon, Georgia, wife of
       Carleton Burke Chapman, No. 34077
    Mrs. Annie Smith Lambdin, born Jacksonville, Georgia,
       wife of William Wallace Lambdin, No. 71726
    Mrs. Vassye Harrell Peacock, born Palmetto, Georgia,
       wife of Levi Milton Peacock, Jr., No. 101147
    Mrs. Agnes Smith Renfroe Roberts, born Richland, Florida,
       wife of G. P. Roberts, No. 101155
    Mrs. Jeanne Lambdin Groves, born Barnesville, Georgia,
       wife of Edward Welsh Groves, No. 525896

          In summary, data from the above applications show the following
information on the Harrell family:

    John Harrell (1746-1799) enlisted 1776 as private in Captain
       John Brown's Company, Col. Francis Nash's regiment of
       North Carolina Militia.  He was born and died in North
       Carolina.  Married Unity Fox.  [The application of Mrs.
       Groves also gives:  "5th North Carolina Regiment, Conti-
       nental Line, commanded by Colonel Francis Work.  Term of
       enlistment 2-1/2 years, which expired on October 6, 1778.
       He was discharged.  See State Records of North Carolina,
       Vol. XVI, page 1072; also see National No. 34202.
       Private, North Carolina Continental Line.]

       Son:  William Harrell (b. 1769)
             m.  Mary (Harrell) (his cousin) b. 1769

             Mrs. Groves states:  "My great-great-grandfather
             was William Harrell who married his first cousin,
             Mary Harrell.  They were both born in the family
             homestead at Lynch's Creek, North Carolina in 1769.
             They were married in 1787."  She states both died
             on or about 1790.]

             Children:

             (l)  Jethro B. Harrell (1789-1883)
                  m. 1st, Nacy Phillips (1795-1861)
                     Son:  Francis Marion Harrell (1822-1886)

             (2)  Agnes Harrell (b. 1790) [Mrs. Groves shows:
                  "born on 1790 at Lynch's Creek North Carolina
                  died at Macon, Georgia on 12-28-1868", Macon, Georgia."]

                  m. 1st, 1810, Darien, Ga., to Lachland McIntosh
                  m. 2nd, 4-26-1820 to George Augustus Smith (2nd wife)




         All of the above D.A.R. records, except the record of Mrs.
Groves (daughter of Mrs. Lambdin) which was secured from D.A.R. Head-
quarters as a current member, were listed in volumes of members who
joined during a period up to the 1920's, and it has not been possible to
date to locate them or any other descendants.

         Mrs. Groves was contacted during June 1972 by Shirley Faucette,
but so far she has not been able to furnish additional information.
During August she suggested that the widow of her cousin, James Alexander
Austin, of Mandarin, Florida, be contacted.  Information from his record
is given below.

"The Southern Genealogist's Exchange Quarterly", Vol. VIII, Winter 1967:

         Mr. Joseph E. Steadman furnished the following information in
his letter of July 18, 1972.  He found that the above publication carried
on pages 9-11 the printed record of the Henry J. Smith (Appling County,
Georgia) family Bible, owned in 1967 by James Alexander Austin of Mandarin,
Florida.  Mr. Austin was a grandson of the original owner and a son of
Virginia (Jennie) Smith Austin.  [In a telephone conversation with Mrs.
Austin on August 11, 1972, she stated that Mr. Austin had died about five
years ago, but that she still has his records and may be able to find
other Harrell data.]

         This record included 11 entries for marriages, 27 entries
for births, and 14 entries for deaths.  Mr. Steadman says:

      "The first entry in the published record, under Marr€ages, shows -
         George A. Smith and Agness [Harrell] McIntosh married in
         McIntosh County Feb. 15th, 1820.

      "The first two entries in the published record, under Births, show -
         George A. Smith born at London, England, Feb. 22d, 1788.
         Agness Harrell born in South Carolina July 27th, 1790.

         Mr. Steadman's analysis of this was as follows:

      "In view of the Bible entry which shows that Agnes (Harrell)
      McIntosh-Smith was born in South Carolina, I am convinced that
      her father was the William Harold (Harrell) listed in the 1790
      census for Richland County, S.C.  Furthermore, I now definitely
      believe that the said William was a brother of the Sarah Harrell
      who married your Henry Fox...."

          It is hoped that Mrs. Austin may find further information among
her husband's papers concerning the make-up of the families of William and
Mary Harrell.

                        * * *


          A "William Harold" (Harrell?) and Henry Fox are listed as
neighbors in the 1790 census for Richland County, S.C. (not completed
until 1792), and William Harold's family included in addition to himself,







                                                                       -

_

                                                                          6a







a young male (possibly Jethro B., b. 1789), and two females (possibly wife
Mary, b. 1769, and daughter Agnes, b. 1790) which would agree with the
data contained in the DAR Lineage Books.

          Whereas Mrs. Grove's D.A.R. application indicates that William
and Mary Harrell both died in 1790 and their daughter was born in that
same year at Lynch's Creek, North Carolina, Mr. Austin's Bible record
shows that their daughter Agness was born July 27, 1790, in South Carolina.

          The location of "Lynch's Creek" is now being investigated and
county records in the areas searched.  The only creek of that name so far
found listed in North Carolina is in the present Franklin County, entering
Tar River slightly north of the county line.  This area was also known as
Bute County from 1764 to 1779, and many Bute County records are now in
Warren County, North Carolina, records.

          If, however, Mr. Austin's records are correct in stating that
Agness Harrell was born in South Carolina, and the family plantation in
1790 was located on Lynch's Creek in that state, it quite likely was that
Lynch's Creek located not far from the home of Henry Fox in Richland
County.  And it is also likely that this William Harrell may have been
that William Harold listed in Henry Fox's neighborhood in the 1790 Richland
County, South Carolina, census, as pointed out by Mr. Steadman.

          In such a case, Sarah Harrell, wife (and cousin) of Henry Fox,
may have been a sister of William and a daughter of John and Unity Fox
Harrell.  In any event, she was doubtless closely related to that family.
A previous search of Richland County records has revealed no other Harrell
information in available sources.  There is no information known at this
time on where the two children, Agness Harrell and Jethro B. Harrell, who
were both under two years of age in 1790, lived following the death of
their parents, given as occurring in 1790.

                        * * *


         These sources all indicate that Unity Fox was the wife of John
Harrell except the item given in 1933 by Mrs. Colson, referred to pre-
viously, which stated:

         "Wm. Harrell (son of Jno.) m Unity Fox N.C."

          It is possible that this research item may have been erroneously
misinterpreted by the copier, and rather than being given as above, perhaps
should have, instead, been punctuated as follows:

          "Wm. Harrell (son of Jno. m Unity Fox N.C.)"

The researcher may have misinterpreted a statement similar to the following
quote from one of the above-mentioned Georgia DAR records:

        "My great-great-great-grandfather, John Harrell, father of
         William Harrell married Unity Fox (records lost)  He was born
         at North Carolina in 1746."  [Underlining by Shirley Faucette]

                                                                         6b



         On the other hand, Mr. Steadman calls attention to the quotation
on page 157 of Volume 2 of Hathaway's North Carolina Historical and Genea-
logical Register:

     "William Harrell married Mary Harrell (lst cousins) children of
     William and John Harrell, they had a brother Hardy."

         In his letter of July 18, 1972, Mr. Steadman advances the follow-
ing possible theory:

     "William Harrell maried Mary Harrell (lst cousins) children
     (RESPECTIVELY -- my interpretation) of William and John Harrell".

     "If my interpretation is correct, this means that William Harrell
     was the son of William Harrell, Sr., and Mary Harrell was the
     daughter of John Harrell.  Mrs. Colson's data (probably based on
     information given in Hathaway recites that: 'William Harrell (son
     of John) md. Unity Fox (N.C.)'.  This, together with the foregoing,
     indicates that William Harrell, Sr. (father of William, Jr.) was a
     brother of John Harrell, Jr. (father of Mary) and that these
     brothers were the sons of one John Harrell, Sr."

                        * * *


         In a letter dated August 27, 1970, Dr. Robinson enclosed the
following comments:

   "Many people of the name Harrell lived in North Carolina in
   Pasquemans, Chowan, Bertie and Northampton counties which were
   situated immediately across the state line from Brunswick, Green-
   ville and Southampton counties, Virginia, wherein William Fox and
   the Avents resided.  The records show that Col. Thomas Avent owned
   property in all these Virginia counties and in Northampton County,
   North Carolina, and that his children and the children of William
   Fox settled in the latter county.

   "Mary Claiborne Fox, daughter of William Fox, married a Johnson
   and lived in Northampton county, N.C.  It is claimed by some
   descendants that she married Benjamin Johnsoh; by other descen-
   dants that she married Thomas Johnson.  In either case she probably
   married a son of Thomas Johnson whose name is mentioned in the will
   of Col. Thomas Avent (signed September 25, 1756):  'I give to my
   son William Avent...the plantation whereon Thomas Johnson lately
   dwelt situated in the county of Northampton and province of North
   Carolina.'

   "It is reasonable to conclude that Noona (Unity?) Fox, the probable
   youngest child of William and Sarah Avent Fox had through her family
   associations made friends among the people of Northampton county
   including the Harrell family, and that it was doubtless she who married
   William [John?] Harrell and had a daughter Sarah Harrell who married
   into the Col. Henry Fox family of South Carolina.  Proof that a William
   Harrell married a Unity Fox is found among a collection of "Virginia

                                                             6c


   Genealogies' now in the Georgia Historical Society, Savannah:
   'William Harrell (son of Jno.) m. Unity Fox N. C.'  The marriage
   took place in North Carolina, probably about the year 1770."
   [Note by Shirley Faucette:  This is the same information previously
   discussed on Page 2 and elsewhere in this section.]

          In commenting further concerning "Noona", Dr. Robinson made the
 following observations after studying a copy of material given to Shirley
 Faucette in July 1970 by Mrs. Josephine Cortner Zeitler Hill of Moores-
 ville, Alabama.  Mrs. Hill (then Zeitler) had copied, by hand, into a
 small notebook a history of the John Fox (son of William Fox of Brunswick
 County) family and its Love descendants, which had been written by the
 late Mrs. Sarah Elizabeth Love Peck, in 1894.  Mrs. Hill obtained this
 material from Mrs. Peck's family during the 1930's.  Dr. Robinson commented:

          "Mrs. Zeitler's material is important in that it contains
   much information about the family of John Fox son of William Fox
   of Brunswick County.  A fault is that Mrs. Peck failed to include
   any facts about births, marriages and deaths - an important
   element in genealogical notes.

          "An interesting item included in her notes concerns four
   of William Fox's eight children:

             'lst, Nuna married Jesse Mitchell
             '2nd, William married Patty Reeves
             '3rd, John married Celia Bonner
             '4th, Sarah married Mr. Robinson'

          "It was not Sarah Fox but Lucy Fox who married Mr. Robinson.
   Might Mrs. Peck not have made a mistake also in claiming that
   Noona Fox married Jesse Mitchell?  And may it not have been Sarah
   Fox, about whom we have found nothing, who married Jesse Mitchell?"

                        * * *

         Abstracts of North Carolina wills by Grimes and Olds, as well as
an entire chapter, Pages 183-206, of Mrs. Smallwood's "Some Colonial and
Revolutionary Families of North Carolina", Volume 2, list many Harrells in
Bertie and other North Carolina counties.  Colonial Bertie County was
later divided into several of the present North Carolina counties.

         The John Harrells and William Harrells are almost as numerous
as the John, William, and Henry Foxes!  None of the Harrells listed has
yet been identified as the husband of Unity Fox.  It is possible that he
is among some of the younger sons listed without mention of a wife.  No
will or other document has been located which names a combination of
brothers John and William with a close relative named "Hardy Harrell" except
in possibly some cases where it is known that the wife was not Unity Fox.
Two or more different men named "Israel Hardy Harrell" are listed, and the
name "Hardy Harrell" appears in later Georgia records.



Exhibit 1                                                    7



     *CHILDREN OF WILLIAM FOX OF BRUNSWICK COUNTY, VIRGINIA


William Fox, b. 1710; d. 1763
Will dated December 22,1763; recorded January 23, 1764
m. 1734, Sarah Avent, b. ca. 1716; d. after August 10, 1779

Children:

1.  Elizabeth (Betty) Fox, b. ca. 1735, d. after 1775
   m. John Rives, b. 1730; d. 1775. No issue.

2.  Lucy Fox, b. ca. 1737, d. before 1801.
   m. William Robinson, b. 1730, d. 1801.
   Children:  Sarah, Rebecca, John, Mary, Daniel, David,
   William, Winifred and Lucy.

3. William Fox, b. 1739; d. November 7, 1798.
   m. Martha Patsy Rives.
   Children:  Winifred, Robert, William, Rebecca, Nancy and
   Uriah Irvine.

4.  John Fox, b. about 1 742, d . 1 795
   m. Celia Bonner
   Children:  Sally, Isaac, Benjamin, John and Margaret Bonner (Peggy).

5.  Mary Claiborne Fox, b. ca. 1745; d.   ?
   m. Benjamin (Thomas?) Johnson
   Children:  Benjamin.

6.  Sarah Fox, b. ca. 1747. No information

7.  Thomas Avent Fox, ca. 1750; d. 1815
   m. (l) Mildred, surname unknown
   Children:  Lavina, James, William, John A., Rebecca, Mildred
   and Thomas.
   m. (2) Mrs. Lavina Smith.  No issue.

8.  Noona (Unity?) Fox, b. ca. 1752.
   m. (probably) ca. 1770, William Harrell.  Had a daughter Sarah Harrell,
   b. 7/30/1772, d. 1848, m. Henry Fox, a grandson of Col. Henry Fox
   of South Carolina.


*Except in the case of William Fox, Jr., all years of birth are conjectures.
Names of children are arranged in probable order of birth, as indicated by
facts known concerning them.  Both estimates are believed to be approximately

             ABSTRACT OF WILL OF WILLIAM FOX


Brunswick County, Virginia, Will Book 4, Page 388.  Dated 12-22-1763.
(Wife Sarah Avent Fox, daughter of Col. Thomas Avent)


I give and bequeath my daughter Betty...one negro girl named...and
one named Abby to her and her heirs forever....

I give and bequeath unto my daughter Lucy Robinson one negro boy
named Tommy to her and her heirs forever....

Also I give and bequeath to my son William Fox the land beginning....

I give unto my son Thomas Avent Fox the land that I hold on the lower
side...to him and his heirs forever...

The plantation I live on I give and bequeath to my son John Fox to
him and his heirs forever....

I give and bequeath to my son William Fox one negro girl named Jane,
one negro girl named Nora (?) negro boy named Frank, cattle belonging
to the south side of the creek one horse named Randolph, one feather bed
and furniture to him and his heirs forever and the hogs up in the....

I give and bequeath to my daughter Mary Johnson one negro boy named
Robin to her and her heirs forever....

Also, I give and bequeath to my son John Fox one negro girl named Amy
one negro named Lucy and one negro boy named Charles to him and his heirs
forever....

I give and bequeath to daughter Sarah Fox one negro boy named Nat (?)
to her and her heirs forever....

I give and bequeath to my daughter Noona Fox the negro boy named Daniel
to her and her heirs forever....

Also I give and bequeath to my son Thomas Avent Fox one negro boy named
Tom and one named Jacob one girl Beck (?) to him and his heirs forever....

I give and bequeath to my son William Fox one negro boy named Dick to
him and his heirs forever....

I give to my daughter Lucy Robinson 20 shillings cash....

Also to my beloved wife Sarah Fox one negro named Great Jimmy and Little
Jimmy and Dinah and all the household goods and stock...my widow after
her...I give and bequeath to my son William Fox Great Jimmy and Dinah to
him and his heirs forever, after her decease....





Will of William Fox of Brunswick Co., Va. (continued)


Also, I give and bequeath to my son John Fox...negro named Little Jimmy
to him and his heirs forever....

I...all my household goods and stock to be sold and divided amongst my
children except William Fox....

And I do likewise constitute and make and ordain Thomas Vinson (?) of
Brunswick Co., and my wife Sarah Fox my only and sole executors of this
my last will and testament....  Signed sealed...by the said William Fox,
his last will and testament in the presence of....


                                            William Fox (seal)


At court held 23rd January 1764, executors were bonded.

Inventory filed Will Book 4, Page 392 and 393.

                                     COLONEL HENRY FOX
          OF CHARLESTON AND RICHLAND COUNTY, SOUTH CAROLINA


          No biographical sketch of Colonel Henry Fox is included
in this section due to the comprehensive material presented by Mr.
Joseph E. Steadman, Sr., beginning on Page 43, Part II, Chapter 4,
of his Ancestry of the Fox Family of Richland and Lexington Counties,
South Carolina.

          Various publications in which Col. Henry Fox is mentioned
that are of special interest are:


Rambles in the Pee Dee Basin, by H. T. Cook.  Pages 63-64.

     "Col. Henry Fox was an eminent lawyer in Charles Town..."

     "Opposite these three land grabbers [Col. Thomas Hume, Col.
     Fox, and Thomas Groom were..."


The Expansion of South Carolina, by R. L. Meriwether.

     Page 100:
     "...sending of Colonel Henry Fox as agent to bring them
     [Catawba Indians] to terms...."

     Page 102:
     "...near the mouth of Colonels Creek, Colonel Henry Fox
     established himself and apparently gave his title to the
     creek.  He had lived in South Carolina four years before
     his mission of 1737 to the Catawbas, and perhaps about
     this time made his home on the Wateree...."

     Page 107:
     "Fox...petitioned for a warrant to the land Cof "the poor
     and illiterate Charles Lindsay"] piously declaring that
     his chief purpose was to remove as a neighbor one whose
     principles were 'Enfattuated by the Common Enemy to man-
     kind'....  But Lindsay vigorously denied all charges of
     actual wrongdoing, and, whatever influence the common
     enemy had over him, kept his land...."


The Catawba Indians - The People of the River, by Douglas Summers Brown.

     Page 165:
     "...Col. Henry Fox, an officer in the Rangers on 'the northern
     frontiers' was given instructions to proceed to the Catawba
     Nation with 'the utmost Expedition..."'

                          WILL OF MARTIN KEANE


(Will not dated; proved October 24, 1738; recorded December 3, 1739;
Charleston, South Carolina.  Recorded in Will Book 1736-40, page 462.)


CAROLINA FS

          IN THE NAME OF GOD AMEN I Martin Keane of English Santee in
the Province aforesaid Indian Trader being Sick and Weak in Body but
of perfect & Sound Memory Do Make & Ordain my Last Will and Testament
in Manner following I Will that my Body be Buried in a Christian like
decent Manner at the Discretion of my Exors# hereafter Named, and as for
What Estate I am pofsefsed of I dispose of in Manner following Vizt
Imprimis I Will that all my Just Debts and Funeral Charges be paid and
discharged afsoon as Pofsible may be and the Remaining part of my Estate
both Real and Personal in this Province in the Creek Nation or Elsewhere
I will that it be Equally Divided and that One half of it be for my
Loveing Wife Martha Keane which Half I Give unto her my said Wife Martha
and to her heirs and Afsigns for Ever As to the other Half I Will that
it be Sold to the Best advantage and Turn'd into Money, that the said
Money be Let Out at Interest upon Bond with Sufficient Security (Such as
Shall be approved of by my Exors# for the use of my Daughter Martha
Keane until She shall Marry or Arrive at the Age of Sixteen Years and
until then the said Interest be called in Yearly and paid her my said
Daughter or her Guardians Towards her Maintainence which other half of
my said Estate I Give and Bequeath in Manner aforesaid unto my said
Daughter and unto her heirs & Afsigns for Ever I Do Nominate and appoint
my said Wife Martha A joint Executrix and Mr John Cragg and Kennedy
O Brien joint Executors with her my said Wife of this my Last Will and
Testament and I do Revoke and annul all other Wills by me heretofore
Made allowing this Only to be my Last Will and Testament


                                              Martin Keane (Seal)

Signed Sealed pronounced published
and Declared in the prefence of Us (the
Words (For Ever) are Interlined twixt
the 14th and 15th Lines) by the Testator
at whose Request We Sign Our Names as Witnefses
hereuntO      Daniel Clark

              Lewis Bynon
              John Wilson

              By the Honble William Bull Esqr presedent and Commander in
Chief in and over his Majesty's province of South Carolina --

              To Daniel Pepper & Thomas Smith Esqr5 or either of them I
Reposing Especial Trust and Confidence in the Integrity care and Circum-
spection of you the said Daniel Pepper & Thomas Smith have by these


                                                                       l

presents do give unto you full power and authority to Examine the Several
Witnefses to the Last Will and Testament of Martin Keane late of this
Province Indian Trader deceased as shall be brought before you upon their
Several Corporal Oaths on the Holy Evangelists of Almighty God touching
the Due Execution of the said Will according to the form of the Statute
in that Case made and provided and also you are to Return your Doings
herein under your hand and Seal for my approbation nd allowance and you
are also to administer the Usual Oath the the Execr  therein Named

                                Given under my hand and Seal this
                                Seventh Day of December Anno Domini 1738

                                        Wm Bull

The Execr Oath

You Swear that you Believe this Instrument of Writing to be the Last Will
and Testament of Martin Keane deceased and that you will well and truly
to administer his goods rights and Credits which appertained and belonged
to him at the time of his Death and that you will pay all and Singular
his Debts and Legacy's as far as his Estate will Extend & the Law Shall
bind You and that you will make a True and perfect Invetory of his Goods
Rights and Credits and return the Same into the Secry's  Office of this
Province according to the time prescribed by Law & in all things behave
your self as an Executor Ought to do

                         So help you God

South Carolina FS

          Personally appeared before me Daniel Pepper Esqr One of his

their Names to it as Evidences also and Kennedy OBrien One of the Exc

                                              Danll Pepper  ##

                              A CHEROKEE WAR DOCUMENT

    "[The following interesting document pertaining to the Cherokee
    war in South Carolina in 1760-61, was recently sent by Mr. A.
    Landfear Norrie, of New York, through Mr. Pembroke Jones, of the
    same city, to Mr. W. D. Porcher, of Charleston, to be by him
    transmitted to Governor McSweeney for the use and benefit of
    students of the history of this State.  Governor McSweeney pre-
    sented it to this Society.]


"George R

           Whereas it appears by the annexed Report of the Comptrollers
of the Accounts of Our Army that the sum of Four thousand five hundred
seventy three pounds ten shillings and four pence is due unto the late
Sir James Colebrook Baronet Arnold Nesbitt Esqr Sir George Colebrooke
Baronet and Moses Franks Esqr for victualling Our Forces within the
Provinces of South Carolina and Georgia with all Species of Provisions
between the 1st day of January 1761 and the 25th day of March following
both daies included Our Will and Pleasure is And We do hereby direct
authorise and command that out of any Monies in your hands that may be
applied to this Service You do pay unto the Representatives of the said
late Sir James Colebrooke and unto the said Arnold Nesbitt Sir George
Colebrooke and Moses Franks or to their Assigns the said sum of Four
thousand five hundred seventy three pounds ten shillings and four pence
upon Account in satisfaction of the like sum due to them as aforesaid
And this shall be as well to You for making such payment as to Our Auditors
and all Others concerned in passing your Accounts for allowing the same
thereupon a sufficient Warrant Given at Our Court at Saint James's this
thirtieth day of July 1761 in the first Year of Our Reign

                                           By his Majesty's Command

                                           HOBER NEWEARTH
                                      GILB:ELLIOT BARRINGTON

To Our Right Trusty and Wellbeloved
Councillor Henry Fox Esqr Paymaster Genl.
of Our Guards Garrisons and Land Forces

    Representatives of the late Sr JaS Colebrooke et al L4573,,10,,4
for vict9 in S° Carolina & Georgia fm 1 Janry to 25 March 1761--

                           G COLEBROOKE Executor Of ye late
                                        Sir James Colebrooke
                           ARNOLD NESBITT
                           G COLEBROOKE
                           MOSES FRANKS

                                                              21



              WILLIAM FOX OF RICHLAND COUNTY, SOUTH CAROLINA


          William Fox, who died in Richland County, South Carolina, in
1816, was the son of Colonel Henry Fox. A letter from Joseph E. Stead-
man, Sr., dated April 27, 1972, gives the following opinions:

    "Reading between the lines of the Fox family sketch, together
    with a modified family tradition, we learn that William Fox (son
    of Henry 3rd) was born about 1743 at his father's plantation on
    or near the Black River in the present Clarendon or Williamsburg
    County, S.C.  During the year 1746 he moved with his father to
    or near Charleston, S.C.  He was too young to have served in the
    Cherokee Indian War of 1759-1760, as did his older brothers
    (Thomas, Henry, and John).  At about 1766, while living in or
    near Charleston, he married Sarah Carroll (perhaps an orphaned
    child  who then was living with her uncle Charles Carroll, a resi-
    dent of that city.) Before or during 1769 he moved to the present
    Richland County, S.C., and settled on land granted to him on
    27 September 1769. His petition for the land was dated 4 April
    1769. One of his sons was Henry Fox, born 12 June 1768 in Rich-
    land County (if not in or near Charleston), who at about 1790
    married Sarah Harrell (b. 29 July 1772)."

           As the exact date of William's birth is not known, and there is
no record as to which of the two wives of Colonel Henry Fox (Mary Goodwyn?
and Mrs. Martha Keen) was his mother, estimates of his birth date have
varied from as early as 1730 to as late as 1744. In a letter to Mrs.
William Ross Brown, dated May 23, 1953, Mr. Steadman had stated that
William Fox was "Born 1730?, in Virginia..."; however, his letter of
October 1, 1956, to Shirley Faucette gave the following explanation:

    "The time - 1730 ? - of William's birth was estimated on the basis
    of a letter written 22 June 1917 by Mrs. Bessie Truly, in which
    she stated that 'he came from Virginia to South Carolina' and that
    he 'left Virginia and settled in South Carolina.'  Mrs. Truly fur-
    ther stated that this information was given to her by her father
    when she was a child [she was born 8-9-1878]. In view of facts
    versus tradition, it is more probable that William was born in
    South Carolina about the year 1737 (as the last child of his
    father's first wife) or in 1739 (as the first child of his father's
    second wife).  His oldest known child, Henry, was born on 12 June
    1768, and William might have been born as late as the year 1744."

          Mr. Steadman's letter of October 30, 1956, stated that it then
seemed more likely that William Fox was born about 1743. His letter of
December 20, 1958, elaborated on these conclusions:

    "William Fox (son of Colonel Henry) evidently was born at some
    time during the year 1743 or 1744, assuming that his son Henry
    (1768-1852) was the first-born child of his parents.  If such
    assumption be correct, then William was a son of his father's

                                                                         22


   second marriage (to Mrs. Martha Keen) and it is safe to state
   that he himself married in 1767 at the age of 23 or 24 years.
   The fact that he performed...strenuous military duty...in 1781
   and 1782 is strong indication that he then was a young man,
   probably in his 30's rather than in his 40's."

          Mrs. Truly, in her booklet on the Fox Family, prepared during
the 1930's or earlier, stated that William Fox "lived to be very old,
probably 80 years, and in his old age took great delight in rehearsing
to his grandsons incidents of the war...."  The information and tradi-
tions that she gives were from old family Bible records and from infor-
mation recalled by her and her half-sister, Mrs. Emma Fox Puthuff.
Mrs. Puthuff was born February 12, 1852, and Mrs. Truly was born
August 9, 1878, both being granddaughters of Thomas Fox, born May 8,
1795, in South Carolina, who was a son of William Fox's oldest son
Henry Fox, and was one of the "grandsons" to whom William Fox recounted
his experiences.  Thomas Fox was about 19 years of age  and his grand-
father was still living when Thomas left South Carolina with his family
about 1814. [See excerpts from Mrs. Truly's work, Part IV, Exhibit 6.]

          If this recollection was correct as to William's living to be
"very old, probably 80 years" at his death in 1816, this would place
his birth around 1736 or 1737, and he could have been the child of his
father's first marriage to Mary Goodwyn.

          Mrs. Eleanor Fox Ponder, in working notes for DAR membership
not completed prior to her death, gave the date of William Fox's birth
as March 19, 1737, but she cited no reference or other means of proof.
She also stated that he "Enlisted in Hillsboro District, S.C. 11th Jan.
1777 (age 40) - Co. Pointers - Service 3 years - Omtd. 1778 - Granted
640 acres of land for 84 months in Colonial Army by law of 1783." This
information is not contained in his military record on file in the
South Carolina Archives, and there is no reference to a Hillsboro Dis-
trict in South Carolina.  Attempts to locate the source of this informa-
tion have not been successful.  In reply to an inquiry from Shirley
Faucette in 1970, the General Services Administration, National Archives
and Records Service, Washington, D.C., advised that they had no pension
file, military service record, or bounty land file for William Fox of
South Carolina, and referred the writer to the South Carolina Department
of Archives.

          No definite dates regarding William Fox himself have been found
prior to the birth of his son Henry, who was born June 12, 1768.

Sarah Carroll Fox, Wife of William Fox

          It is now generally agreed that William Fox was married but
once, and that his wife was a Miss Sarah Carroll, in accordance with
traditional statements of members of the family in Mississippi.  It is
said that she may have been a cousin of her husband, William Fox, and
traditionally she was referred to as being a kinsman, possibly "a niece
and adopted daughter" or "cousin" of Charles Carroll.  This has been
assumed, perhaps erroneously, to have been Charles Carroll of Carrollton,
Maryland.  [See letter dated 1902 from Priscilla Virqinia Fox Starr, and
letter dated 1904 from Carl Fox, both in Section IV.



          Mrs. Truly included this statement in her genealogy:

          "The supposition that Sarah Carroll was daughter of Daniel
    Carroll, is incorrect, since he was born 1756.  I do not know
    name of her father, but I remember hearing my father say many
    times:  'William Fox married his Cousin Sarah Carroll, niece of
    Charles Carroll.'  May have been a cousin of Charles Carroll."


          In his letter dated October 1, 1956, Mr. Steadman stated:

          "In view of the tradition recited by the several descendants
    of Henry Fox, it appears quite probable that his mother, the wife
    of William, was a Miss Carroll whose name might or might not have
    been 'Sarah'.  However, despite tradition, it is almost a certainty
    that William married in South Carolina and not in Maryland.  The
    Carroll family of Richland County, S.C., apparently came there with
    William's father, Henry, from Brunswick County, Va.  The land
    granted to William on 4 September 1770 previously had been granted
    to Edward Carroll, and Carroll had allowed the grant to lapse."

          Mr. Steadman's letter dated December 20, 1958, gave further
opinions concerning this relationship:

          "William Fox and Charles Carroll (1737-1832) were nearly the
    same age, and if the aforementioned kinship existed it seems most
    likely that William's wife was a cousin of Charles.  The Jacob
    Carroll, Sr., who is mentioned in my letter to you under date of
    30 October 1956 was about the same age as William Fox, and these
    two served together in similar duty under the same officers for
    several months during the Revolutionary War.  It is now my strong
    belief that William's wife was a sister of this Jacob Carroll,
    Sr....


          A will dated 1752 for Charles Carroll of Charleston [see
 Exhibit 5]  names "the children of Martin Carroll by my sister Sarah of
 Droghadie, Kingdom of Ireland".  Also named in the will is his wife Esther
 and daughter, Henrietta.  An account of the marriage of Miss Henrietta
 Carroll, at Charleston, South Carolina, is shown in Exhibit 5, also.
 However, no further mention has been found of Martin Carroll, his wife
 Sarah Carroll Carroll, or the children who were not named in the will.  It
 is known that when Henry Fox "of the province of North Carolina" sold 555
 acres of land in Brunswick County, Virginia, that it adjoined land of John
 Carroll.  In this connection, and for Mr. Steadman's theory concerning a
 possible daughter of Henry Fox (2nd), possibly named Unity, marrying John
 Carroll, see Part III, Chapter 3, Page 34, of Mr. Steadman's Ancestry of
 The Fox Family, etc.



                                                                         24




          The will of Jacob Carroll, Sr., (dated April 14, 1815 and proved
June 21, 1815, Richland County, S.C., Will Book "E", p. 309) does not
name his wife, but lists the followi-ng children:  William, James, Jacob,
Joseph, John, and Unity (married Joseph Collins).

          Similarly, the will of William Carrell, dated January 21, 1835,
and proved April 6, 1835, recorded in Will Book K, Page 47, included a
daughter Unity who married        Gray.

          If this Jacob and this William were brothers of Sarah Carroll,
as seems likely, the fact that each had daughters named Unity (a frequent
name in the Fox Family) may indicate that the "cousin" relationship
between Sarah Carroll and her husband William Fox was through the Fox
line rather than through William's mother, whose identity is not proved.

          Possible Carroll relationships are outlined further in
Exhibit 4 of this section.


Discarded Theories Concerning Sarah Carroll

          Referring again to Mr. Steadman's letter dated December 20, 1958,
he states:

          "It is only through Dr. Benjamin T. Carter that the name of
    William's wife is given (doubtless without reference to his family
    records) as 'Barbara'.  This evidently is in error, since his
    ancestress (Unity Fox) married Robert Carter who was the son of
    Henry and Barbara Carter; therefore 'Barbara' was Unity's mother-
    in-law and not her mother.  Henry Carter's will (1 November 1785 -
    5 December 1785), witnessed by William Fox, names his wife Barbara
    and his children (one of whom was Robert).  Barbara Carter (widow)
    is listed as a next-door neighbor of William Fox in the 1790 census
    for Richland County, S.C."

          Much other traditional information has been written, and much
of it has later been found to be incorrect.  A letter dated December 4,
1904, (See Exhibit 3, Section IV) from Carl Fox (1876-1958) to Eleanor
Fox Ponder, stated that Sarah Carroll was a widow with twin sons before
her marriage to William Fox:

          "William's wife was a widow when he married her, with two
    sons - I think twins - named Elisha and Elijah and they were very
    wild and dissolute and spent everything their mother and William
    owned."

          Mrs. Eleanor Fox Ponder also indicated in her records that
William's wife was a widow, perhaps named McLeod, when he married her
and that she had twin sons, Elisha and Elijah.  She apparently based
this theory partly on the above information from Mr. Carl Fox, addressed
to her in 1904.



                                                                          25



          In this connection, Mr. Steadman's letter of December 20,
 1958, stated:

          "The sources which state that William's wife was a widow
    (uncertainly named 'McLeod')with two, or twin, children when he
    married her evidently are in error and have confused the matter
    with the situation as regards Henry Fox [this should be Thomas
    Fox, 1795-1876, grandson of William] who married the widow
    Brent, she then having one or two living children (had a total
    of four, two of whom were twins).  As to the name 'McLeod', this
    doubtless is a confusion arising from the fact that the twin sons
    Elijah and Elisha Fox were buried at Good Hope Methodist Church
    [should be Baptist near the present McLeod's Chapel in Richland
    County, S.C."


          It seems certain that the twins Elijah and Elisha could not
have been children of Sarah Carroll by a previous marriage, since
William and Sarah's son Henry, was born 1768, and the twins were born
in 1789.  They are named as "sons" in William Fox's will in 1808, and
were later named as Executors of the large estate which William Fox
left, being referred to as "the principal legatees".  Tombstones at
their graves, which are in the same plot with Unity Fox Carter, con-
firm the birth date of 1789.


Land Records for William Fox

          In A History of Richland County; South Carolina, by Edwin L.
Green, William Fox iS iste  as an ear y  andowner, wit  lands near
that which his father had acquired earlier.  Here it is shown that
Henry Fox, father of William Fox, was granted 100 acres on September 11,
1764, located on Second Creek and adjoining the property of John Griffin.
Grants for William Fox included 100 acres of land, April 4, 1769, which
had previously been granted to Warren Jackson on March 11, 1767, and 100
acres on September 4, 1770, which had previously been granted to Edward
Carroll on April 24, 1767   This land was situated in the southeastern
corner of Richland County, in the fork of the Wateree River and the
Congaree River.

          See Exhibit 60f this Section for sketches of land surveyed
for William Fox.  These sketches and descriptions were copied from
records on file in the South Carolina Department of Archives and History
in July 1970 by Mrs. Emma Shirley Faucette and Shirley Faucette.  Copies
were not made of all grants, memorials, etc., on record, but only of
representative plats.  Other grants listed in Green's History of Richland
County, South Carolina, describe land of other persons as adjoining the
land of Henry Fox or William Fox.  These include land for Thomas Ferguson,
Lester Andrews, Isaac Hill, Richard S(h)ingleton, and Absalom Griffin.
Land for the latter was described as adjoining Henry Fox's estate on
September 8, 1770, whereas land for Isaac Hill was described on February 4,
1770,as adjoining Henry Fox.  It is presumed that Henry Fox died on some
date between February 4 and September 8 of 1770.

                                                                         26



         Other persons whose land descriptions are in the same general
area as that of Henry Fox and William Fox, e.g., naming McCord's Ferry,
Colonel's Creek, Allison's Path, etc., included:

         Edmund Carroll, 100 acres, September 1, 1770
         Jacob Carroll, 100 acres, September 11, 1770
         Andrew Allison, 100 acres, April 5, 1763, and
                         500 acres, January 14, 1773
         John Cook, 100 acres, September 12, 1770
         Samuel Scott, January 6, 1759 and March 6, 1770
         Richard Wayne, 450 acres, December 14, 1769
         Several Goodwyn men are mentioned during the
             period 1765 to 1773 in this area.

         On May 1, 1775, William Fox of Camden District, S.C., is
recorded as transferring to Capt. John Russell 100 acres of land (part
of 250 acres) in Craven County in the fork of the Wateree and Congaree
Rivers. Mr. Steadman, in his letter dated October 1, 1956, to Shirley
Faucette, stated that the deed was signed by William Fox alone, which
could have indicated that he then had no wife, otherwise she would have
signed away her dower right; but his letter of December 20, 1958, cor-
rected this assumption by stating that "it appears that the county
clerks (perhaps following a careless custom or being indifferent) did
not record the release of dower in many instances where the husbands
sold property while their wives were still living."


Military Service in the American Revolution

                                                                                      l

         William Fox served as a soldier in the American Revolution
with his service recorded in Chapter 7, "The Revolution", of A History
of Richland County, by Edwin L. Green, as follows:

    "Fox, William. 1781, thirty days at Ancrum's under Capt. John Cook;
                   1782, 183 days at McCords Ferry under Capt. John McCord;
                         33 days at Orangeburg under Capt. Willis Whitaker,
                         Horseman."

His military record, typed by Shirley Faucette from the handwritten copy
on file in the South Carolina Department of Archives and History, Columbia,           3
South Carolina, is shown in Exhibit 7. A photostat of this record was
obtained but it was illegible, and parts of the original also could not be
read.

         An interesting traditional story of his revolutionary service is
contained in excerpts previously referred to from the account of Mrs.
Bessie Fox Truly, included in Exhibit 6 of Section IV.

         According to Joseph E. Steadman, he is also listed as "William
Fox (F. 142) horseman, cattledriver and assistant to the Quartermaster,
1781-82" in Spirit of Patriotism - Revolutionary & Ancestral Records, Sons
of the Revolution, California, p. 367.



                                                             27




Children of William Fox

          William Fox's will, dated April 13, 1808, was sworn to
June 20, 1816, filed July 1, 1816, and recorded in Will Book G, pp. 3
and 4, of Richland County, South Carolina, records.  See Exhibit 1,
Page 29,  for a copy of this will.  Also included is a document in
which Henry Fox, son of William Fox, and Robert Carter, son-in-law
of William, renounce their executorship of William's will to his other
sons, Elisha and Elijah Fox.

          In his will, William Fox names his children in the following
order.  The birth dates, where known, are given below:

   Henry Fox                    Born June  12,  1768   Died Jan 18, 1852
   Ann (Scott)                  -                      Died prior to April 1808*
   Unity (Carter)               Born Oct.  28,  1781   Died Jan. 16, 1870
   Mary (Powell)                                       Died after April 1808*
   El izabeth (Kill ingsworth)                         Died prior to April 1808*
   El i jah                     Born  May 1 6,  1 789  Di ed Apri 1 23, 1 863
   Elisha                       Born  May 16,   1789   Died Feb. 6, 1862

                                                       *date of the will

          The 1790 census for "Camden District, Richland County, S.C.",
lists William Fox as head of a household consisting of one male over 16,
three males under 16, and 2 females.  Since Henry Fox, his oldest known
son, is listed separately, it is presumed that at the time of the 1790
census William had three sons living at home, one of whom is apparently
not named in William's will made in April 1808, and presumably died
prior to that time.  [See Mr. Steadman's explanation on page 57 of his
book, concerning the South Carolina 1790 census not being completed until
February 1792. ]

          The 1810 census for Richland County, shows that William Fox then
had one male 45 and up (presumably himself) and one male 16 to 26 then
living at home.  No females were listed.  Eight slaves were listed, making
a total of ten persons in his household.

          Mr. Steadman, in his letter to Shirley Faucette dated December 20,
1 958, stated :

          "We have only the 1790 and 1810 census records [1800 census
    lost or destroyed and the will of William Fox as sources of infor-
    mation concerning the number of his children.  The will might or
    might not name the children in order according to age; however, it
    doubtless is the case that several other children were born and
    died in infancy or childhood, before their father's will was made
    on 13 April 1808, and these other children should be identified
    with the presumed missing birth dates between the years 1768 and
    1 789 . "



_



                                                                                     28



                      If the daughters were listed in William's will in order of
            age, three daughters (including Unity Fox Carter, whose birth date in
            1781 is known) would have been under nine or ten years of age at the
            time of the 1790 census.  All presumably would have been living at
            home, as well as their mother, if she were still living, making a
            otal of four females.  However, only two females are listed in that
            census, one presumably being Unity Fox Carter, then nine or ten years
            of age, and the only daughter whose birth date is known.

                      Since, at the time William Fox's will was made in April 1808,
            (18 years after the 1790 census was made), two of William Fox's daughters,
            Ann Fox Scott and Elizabeth Fox Killingsworth are known to have already
            married, had children, and died, it seems probable that some of his daugh-
            ters were older than indicated by the above order, and were already mar-
            ried prior to the 1790 census.  This could leave daughter Unity and wife
            Sarah to be listed in the 1790 census.  In the event Sarah had died
            within a year or two following the birth of her twin sons (who were 21
            years younger than the oldest known child, Henry), another daughter may
            have remained at home, accounting for the two females listed in the 1790
            census.

                      In addition to those daughters listed in William's will, cir-
            cumstantial evidence indicates that there was another daughter, Sarah,
            possibly the oldest, who was the wife of George Carter, whose will is
            shown in Exhibit 3, Page 41, along with a letter written by Mrs.
            Russell A. Lewis, of Abilene, Texas, setting forth reasons for this
            belief.  Information is also given here indicating that Mary Fox, who
            is shown in William's will as being married to         Powell, may have
            first married John Cooner and been the mother of three children before
            George Carter's will was written in 1802.  Mr. Leonardo Andrea, to whom
            Mrs. Lewis refers, was a well-known South Carolina historian and
            genealogist.

                      Based on these conjectures, and if Henry was the oldest or
            next oldest child of William and Sarah Carroll Fox, their children
            could have been born approximately as follows:

          ?Sarah (Carter)            ?Born            ?Married and died before 1802
          Henry                       Born 6-12-1768   Di ed 1-18-1852
          Ann (Scott)                 Born about 1770  Married and died before  1808
          Mary (?Cooner) (Powell )   Born  about 1772  Married before 1808 (or  1802)
          Elizabeth (Killingsworth)  Born  about 1774  Married and died before  1808
          Son (William?)             Born  about 1776  Died after 1790
          Unity (Carter)             Born  10-28-1781  Died 1-16-1870; married  1798
          Elijah                     Born  5-16-1789   Died 4-23-1863
          Elisha                     Born  5-16-1789   Died 2-16-1862


                      A search of the 1790 and 1810 census records, together with
            abstracts of wills and information given in Green's History of Richland
            Countv, South Carolina, revealed the make-up of various Carter, Scott,
            and related families as shown in Exhibit 2, Page 34, of this section.
            The 1800 census is not available, having been lost or destroyed.

                     WILL OF WILLIAM FOX


(Will dated April 13, 1808; filed July 1, 1816; recorded in Will Book G,
Pages 3 and 4, Richland County, South Carolina.)


State of S° Carolina)   In the Name of God Amen.
Richland District

         I William Fox of the State and District aforesaid Planter,
being weak in body but of Sound Mind and Memory Blessed be God, for the
Same, And Calling to mind the uncertainty of human life, and that it is
appointed for all men once to Die, do make and ordain this my Last Will
and testament, in manner and form following   Viz  I commit my Soul to
God in Hopes of obtaining Mercy thro' Christ for all my past sins and
wickedness, and Body to the earth to be Decently Interred at the Discre-
tion of my ExecurS  hereafter mentioned, and for what Worldly Good it
hath pleased God to bless me with in this Life I give and bequeath the
following manner.

Imprimis it is my Desire that all my just debts shall be paid.  2dly I
give and bequeath unto my Son Henry Fox the sum of Two hundred Dollars.
3dly I give and bequeath unto the children of my late daughter Ann Scott
the Sum of One hundred Dollars to be equaly to be Divided among them.
4thly I give and bequeath unto my Daughter Unity Carter and her heirs the
sum of Two hundred Dollars.  5thly I give and bequeath unto my Daughter
Mary Powell and her heirs the sum of One hundred Dollars.  6tnly I give
and bequeath unto the two children of my late Daughter Elizth Killings-
worth the sum of Two Hundred Dollars Each to be paid by my Execurs unto
them when they shall obtain to the age of twenty one years. #### Turn over

Lastly I Give and Bequeath unto my two Sons Elijah and Elisha and their
Heirs for ever all my Personal Estate consisting of Negroes, Cattle,
Horses, Hogs etc.  Likewise all the Lands that I may Die Possessed of,
Houses & Household furniture I give and bequeath in like manner unto my
two said Sons and their heirs for Ever.  The said Personal & Real Estate
to be Equaly Shared among my Said Sons.  And I do nominate and appoint my
Son Henry Fox and Robert Carter ExecurS of my Last Will and Testament.
Revoking all other wills acknowledging this only to be my Last will and
testament.  In witness whereof I have

      ESTATE PAPERS OF WILLIAM FOX, RICHLAND COUNTY, S.C.


State of S. Carolina)

Richland District   )   Whereas by the last will and Testament of my
                       father William Fox, deceased, Robert Carter
                       and myself were appointed Executors, I am now
                       living over the Mountains and hath for some time lived there, so that
                       it is Quite Inconvenient for me to act in behalf of his Property, and
                       as neither Robert Carter or myself have never Qualified as Executors
                       we therefore give up all right of Executorship unto Elisha and Elijah
                       Fox for them to qualify & take upon themselves (being of age) the
                       Burthen of settling the Estate which may be easily done as every
                       Legacy is specified in the will, and both of them are the principal
                       Legatees.

                                        Given under our hands this
Acknowledged before me )                6th day of Dec- 1816

Rich. Brown, L. U.                                    Henry Fox


      I Robert Carter named Executor in the will of William Fox,
deceased do also renounce the Executorship - Given under my hand
this 4th day of January 1817.
                                                his
Robert                                                X Carter
Witness                                         mark

  Alex T. Herbemont



      Above regarding the will of William Fox (1743-1816) which was
made 4-13-1808, filed (presented ?) 6-20-1816, recorded Book G,
Page 3, File 10-245, Richland County, S.C.

      His son Henry, originally named as executor, was born in this
county 6-12-1768, m ca 1790 to Sarah Harrell and they had moved about
1814 to Cocke Co., East Tenn., just over the "biggest" hump of the
Great Smokey Mountains where they and their families were living when
the father William died and Henry had evidently made a trip back to
Richland County where he executed the above document and he was not
joking when he said "I am now living over the Mountains"!

Exhibit 2                                                                 34



POSSIBLE MAKE-UP OF VARIOUS CARTER, SCOTT, CARROLL AND RELATED FAMILIES
        BASED ON WILLS, CENSUS DATA, AND MISCELLANEOUS SOURCES


Ann Fox Scott

         Ann Fox Scott died prior to the date of her father's will,
April 13, 1808, and he makes a bequest "unto the children of my late
daughter Ann Scott...."

         It is likely that Ann Fox is the Mrs. Ann Scott for whom a
"citation" was issued October 26, 1795, as administrator, along with
George Scott, of the estate of William Scott of Richland County, South
Carolina.  Both Green's HistorY of Richland Countv, South Carolina and
Meriwether's The Expansion of South Carolina state that William Scott
was an early settler in that area.  On Page 103 of Meriwether's book
he states that William Scott married the widow of James McCrellas, so
it is probable that Ann Fox was his second wife and that the George
Scott who was also named as an administrator of the estate was her
step-son.  William Scott, Jr., David McCord, and Joel Adams are listed
as appraisers of the estate.  The citation referred to is filed in the
bcx with the will of William Scott (2nd), Will Book E, p. 196, but the
reldtionship of the younger William Scott is not given.  The wills of
William Scott (2nd) and William Scott (3rd) give numerous family rela-
tionships, but there is no mention of any brothers or sisters for
William Scott (2nd), and it is not known to whom William Fox referred
as "the children of my late daughter Ann Scott".

         The following information is summarized from abstracts of
wills contained in Green's  History of Richland County, South Carolina:


ANN (FOX ?)

m.  William Scott (married first to widow of James McCrellas)
    d. prior to 10-26-1795 when "citation" was issued for appointment
    of Mrs. Ann Scott and George Scott as administrators of estate.
    (Will Book C, p. 124).  Appointed 1-5-1796.  Property appraised
    by William Sco'ct, Jr., David McCord, Joel Adams).  Citation is
    filed in box with will of William Scott, Will Book E, p. 196.

    Children of William Scott:

  ?1.  George Scott  (son or brother?  Named as administrator of
                     William Scott's estate, along with Mrs. Ann Scott.
                     One George Scott is mentioned as being a member
                     of Beulah Baptist Church in Richland County on
                     4-26-1806--see page 128 of Green's History, etc.

Ann Fox Scott (Continued)


          The 1790 Richland County Census listed two William Scotts,
presumably William Scott (2nd) and William Scott (3rd).  They are
shown with the following households:

          3 males 16 and up; 2 males under 16; 4 females.  And,

          1 male  16 and up; 3 males under 16; 4 females; 26 slaves.

William Scott (3rd) does not refer to a wife or children in his will,
and no deductions have been made from these figures.

          It seems unlikely to this writer that "Mrs. Ann Scott"
would have been appointed administrator for the estate of William
Scott (lst), along with George Scott, if she were not his widow.
However, it may have been that she was the wife of-h-s son William (2nd),
and that this was a contributing factor to the "citatio-referred to
above having been filed with the estate papers of William (2nd).  Also,
she may have been the wife of George Scott, of whom no further mention
has been found except as listed.

          Ann Fox Scott, daughter of William Fox was shown as "late
daughter Ann Scott" in his will dated 1808, but it is chronologically
possible, from the few known dates available, for her to have been
the living wife in 1806 of William Scott (2nd).

          In any event, she would have been of legal age in 1795 to
serve as administrator of the estate.


Mary Fox (Cooner?) Powell


          No information has been found in addition to that shown on
Page 28 of this section and in Exhibit 3.



Sarah (Fox?) Carter


          No information has been found in addition to that shown on
Page 28 of this section and in Exhibit 3

Unity Fox Carter

          Unity Fox Carter was born October 28, 1781, and died on
January 16, 1870.  She was married to Robert Carter, born 1770, died 1822.
Unity Fox is the only daughter of William and Sarah Carroll Fox whose
birth and death dates are known, or whose husband's name is known.

          In 1960 and again in July 1970, Shirley Faucette and Emma
Shirley Fox Faucette visited the cemetery at Good Hope Baptist Church
in the Middleboro Community east of Columbia, and saw the markers
there in memory of Unity Carter CinscriPtion, "The righteous shall be
in everlasting remembrance") and of her twin brothers Elijah and
Elisha Fox, all located in the same plot.  John Henry Fox, Jr., also
visited the cemetery subsequent to 1962 and was told by long-time
residents of the area that the highway was built over a portion of
the cemetery.  It is likely that William Fox and others of his family
were buried there, also.

          Information from "The First James Settlers", author not named,
was given by a James family connection, Mrs. Homer White Lockett, of
Eastover, South Carolina, to John Henry Fox, Jr., at the time of his
visit.  Eastover is in the same general area as Middleboro, east of
Columbia.  This material gives a history of the descendants of William
James, who is said to have come to South Carolina from Ireland and
settled near Kings Tree about 1734.  A descendant, Benjamin Albert
James, married Gracie Ann Bates, daughter of Elizabeth (Carter) and
John Bates.  Elizabeth Carter, the second wife of John Jack) Bates,
was born April 28, 1798, and was the daughter of Unity (Fox) and Robert
Carter.  She is said to be buried in the "Scott graveyard".

          The following items are given under a heading "Fox Family":

    "l - Fox was killed by Cherokee Indians and effects taken
            Had a son
    "2 - William Fox - Married Barbara - ?
            (You will find in Columbia, S.C., Book G - p. 3,
             April 13, 1808)
            Buried:  Good Hope Baptist Church
            Was a Revolutionary Patriot."


          This information contained in the copy given to John H. Fox, Jr.,
 is not accurate concerning the Foxes in the following respects:

    1 - "Fox" who was killed by Cherokee Indians was the brother and
        not the father of William Fox  [See Page 55 of Mr. Steadman's
        book.]

    2 - William Fox married Sarah Carroll and not "Barbara 
        Barbara was Henry Carter's wife, as discussed on Page 24
        of this section.

Unity Fox Carter (Continued)


         In listing the children of William Fox, Henry is shown as a
"Revolutionary Patriot".  He was only a small boy during the Revolu-
tion, having been born in 1768.

         Elizabeth Fox, daughter of William Fox, is shown as marrying
"Killingsworth (No children)".  The will of William Fox refers to the
"tw children of mY late dauhter Elizth Killinqsworth".



         An outline of a possible Carter genealogy has been prepared by
Shirley Faucette from the above information, from the wills of Henry
Carter and George Carter, and from the 1790 census for Richland County,
South Carolina.  It is not clear whether John Carter, father of Henry
Carter, had other children, but it appears that in addition to Henry,
he was the father of three other children, as shown.  Information is
from the James history except where indicated otherwise.

          Green's History of Richland Cou, Page 48, gives the following
on Killingsworths in his chapter on ''Early Families":

    "KILLINGSWORTH.  Jacob and Jesse Killingsworth settled in the
    lower part of the county before the Revolutionary War, in which
    Jacob served as a Lieutenant.  With Jesse Killingsworth (1770-
    1856), whose grave is at his old home near Eastover, this family
    name disappeared in the County.  His daughter Dorian married
    William Macfeat."

    [A penciled notation in a copy oP this boGk in the Mississippi
    Department of Archives and History, Jackson, Miss., says:
    "See Rose Family of Miss."]

                                                              40


Elizabeth Fox Killinsworth (Continued)

          On Page 304 of Green's History of Richland County, is a record
of an inventory being made of the estate of a William Killingsworth by
A. B. Joyner, William Whitner, and Jacob Killingsworth on March 13, 1835,
but no further information is given on William Killingsworth.

          An older Jacob Killingsworth than that indicated on Page 48,
is given as Executor in 1793 of the will of Pettigrew Salisbury, and he
evidently was the husband of Salisbury's daughter, Mary.  Mary Killings-
worth and Jesse Killingsworth were, in turn, appointed administrators of
Jacob's estate, and Jacob appears to have been the father of the Jesse
(1770-1856) referred to above.  It is interesting to note that the younger
Jesse is buried at Eastover, which is a community in the same general area
east of Columbia as the Good Hope Baptist Church, where Unity Fox Carter
and the twin brothers Elisha and Elijah are buried.  Mary Salisbury
Killingsworth is said to have married second to Isom Woodward.

          Boddie in his Historical Southern Families, Volume 1, suggests
that William Killingsworth of Surry County, Va., (d. 1709) whose wife
was Avis     (she m. 2 to John Cook), had a daughter Lucy and sons
William (2nd) and John Killingsworth.  William (2nd) was the father of
sons John and William (3rd).  William (3rd) was thought to be the
father of Mary, Priscilla, John, Jesse, and Jacob who married Mary
Salisbury.

          Jacob and Mary Salisbury Killingsworth are listed as the
parents of the following children:  Jesse (1770-1856); Sarah (b ca 1772),
m. John Hill; Mary (Polly) m. William Crockett; Margaret (d 1838) m.
Ephriam Adams of Richland County; Mark (d 7-29-1840), m. Nancy Shell;
Noel (b 1778, d 7-3-1831) m. Jane Scott of Richland County; Jacob, Jr.
(wife unknown) who had children Edward Killingsworth, and Martha Killings-
worth who married Peter Gaffney and had 5 children; and Anne (Nancy),
m. Green Williams (b 1775, d 3-31-1838).

          Jesse, the brother of Jacob who married Mary Salisbury, may be
that Jesse whose will was made June 19, 1818, proved July 3, 1818, and is
recorded in Will Book C, Page 69, Box 17, Package 415.  He mentions "my
six children, viz. Nancy, Elizabeth, Mary, Jesse, Jenny, and Martha" and
names as Executor "my loving son-in-law John McLean and Nancy Killings-
worth, my daughter".  No wife is mentioned.

          The fact that Jacob Killingsworth (Jr.) had two children, and
the name of his wife was not known in Boddie's listing, leads to specu-
lation that his wife may have been Elizabeth Fox, who died prior to the
date of her father William Fox's will (4-13-1808) in which he left a sum
of money "unto the two children of my late Daughter Elizth Killingsworth".
